     1â†’# Session 6: Graph-Based RAG (GraphRAG)
     2â†’
     3â†’In Sessions 1-5, you built sophisticated vector-based RAG systems with intelligent chunking, optimized search, query enhancement, and comprehensive evaluation. But when users ask complex questions like "What technologies do companies that partner with Apple use in automotive manufacturing?", you discover vector RAG's fundamental limitation: it finds similar content, but can't reason about relationships between entities.
     4â†’
     5â†’This session transforms your RAG system from similarity matching to knowledge reasoning. You'll build graph-based architectures that capture entities, relationships, and hierarchical knowledge structures, enabling multi-hop reasoning that connects disparate information through logical pathways. The goal is moving from "find similar documents" to "understand and traverse knowledge relationships."
     6â†’
     7â†’## Optional Deep Dive Modules
     8â†’
     9â†’- **[Module A: Advanced Graph Algorithms](Session6_ModuleA_Advanced_Algorithms.md)** - Advanced graph algorithms and traversal techniques
    10â†’- **[Module B: Production GraphRAG](Session6_ModuleB_Production_Systems.md)** - Enterprise-ready GraphRAG implementation
    11â†’
    12â†’![RAG Architecture Overview](images/RAG-overview.png)
    13â†’
    14â†’The key insight is that knowledge isn't just about content similarity â€“ it's about the relationships between concepts, entities, and facts. A question about Apple's automotive partnerships requires understanding: (1) who Apple partners with, (2) which of those partners work in automotive, (3) what technologies those automotive partners use. Vector RAG can find documents about each piece, but can't connect them logically.
    15â†’
    16â†’GraphRAG solves this by representing knowledge as a graph where nodes are entities/concepts and edges are relationships, enabling traversal through logical reasoning pathways.
    17â†’
    18â†’## NodeRAG Architecture
    19â†’
    20â†’NodeRAG uses specialized node types and heterogeneous graph structures to enable sophisticated multi-hop reasoning and coherent knowledge retrieval.
    21â†’
    22â†’---
    23â†’
    24â†’## Part 1: NodeRAG - Structured Brain Architecture
    25â†’
    26â†’The challenge with vector RAG is that it treats all content uniformly â€“ a company name gets the same representation type as a concept or relationship. But knowledge has inherent structure: entities have attributes, relationships have directionality, and concepts have hierarchies. NodeRAG addresses this by creating specialized node types that preserve the semantic structure of different knowledge components.
    27â†’
    28â†’This isn't just theoretical improvement â€“ it enables reasoning capabilities that are impossible with flat vector representations.
    29â†’
    30â†’```
    31â†’Traditional RAG: Document â†’ Chunks â†’ Uniform Embeddings â†’ Similarity Search
    32â†’NodeRAG: Document â†’ Specialized Nodes â†’ Heterogeneous Graph â†’ Reasoning Pathways
    33â†’```
    34â†’
    35â†’### NodeRAG Key Features
    36â†’
    37â†’1. **Specialized Node Types**: Six distinct node types for different knowledge structures
    38â†’2. **Three-Stage Processing**: Decomposition â†’ Augmentation â†’ Enrichment
    39â†’3. **Personalized PageRank**: Semantic traversal following knowledge relationships
    40â†’4. **HNSW Integration**: Similarity edges within graph structure
    41â†’5. **Reasoning Pathways**: Multi-hop logical reasoning capabilities
    42â†’
    43â†’### NodeRAG's Six Specialized Node Types
    44â†’
    45â†’1. **Semantic Unit Nodes** - Abstract concepts and themes
    46â†’   - Example: "Supply Chain Management" connecting related methodologies
    47â†’
    48â†’2. **Entity Nodes** - Concrete entities with rich metadata
    49â†’   - Example: "Apple Inc." with subsidiaries and partnerships
    50â†’
    51â†’3. **Relationship Nodes** - Explicit connections with evidence
    52â†’   - Example: "Partnership" linking Apple and Foxconn with details
    53â†’
    54â†’4. **Attribute Nodes** - Properties and characteristics
    55â†’   - Example: "Revenue: $394.3B" with temporal information
    56â†’
    57â†’5. **Document Nodes** - Original source segments
    58â†’   - Example: SEC filing containing partnership disclosures
    59â†’
    60â†’6. **Summary Nodes** - Cross-document synthesis
    61â†’   - Example: "Apple Automotive Strategy" synthesizing multiple sources
    62â†’
    63â†’### The Three-Stage NodeRAG Processing Pipeline
    64â†’
    65â†’#### Stage 1: Graph Decomposition
    66â†’
    67â†’NodeRAG performs multi-granularity decomposition that creates specialized node types based on knowledge structure:
    68â†’
    69â†’```python
    70â†’def noderag_decomposition(document):
    71â†’    """NodeRAG Stage 1: Multi-granularity knowledge decomposition"""
    72â†’
    73â†’    # Parallel specialized extraction
    74â†’    semantic_units = extract_semantic_concepts(document)     # Abstract themes and topics
    75â†’    entities = extract_canonical_entities(document)          # People, orgs, locations with metadata
    76â†’    relationships = extract_typed_relationships(document)     # Explicit connections with evidence
    77â†’    attributes = extract_entity_properties(document)         # Quantitative and qualitative properties
    78â†’    document_nodes = create_document_segments(document)      # Contextual source information
    79â†’
    80â†’    return {
    81â†’        'semantic_units': semantic_units,
    82â†’        'entities': entities,
    83â†’        'relationships': relationships,
    84â†’        'attributes': attributes,
    85â†’        'document_nodes': document_nodes
    86â†’    }
    87â†’```
    88â†’
    89â†’#### Stage 2: Graph Augmentation
    90â†’
    91â†’This stage builds the heterogeneous graph structure by creating specialized connections between different node types:
    92â†’
    93â†’```python
    94â†’def noderag_augmentation(decomposition_result):
    95â†’    """NodeRAG Stage 2: Heterogeneous graph construction"""
    96â†’    
    97â†’    # Create typed connections between specialized nodes
    98â†’    semantic_entity_links = link_concepts_to_entities(
    99â†’        decomposition_result['semantic_units'],
   100â†’        decomposition_result['entities']

  2683â†’

  2696â†’                'content': ctx['content'],

  2698â†’                'type': 'vector_similarity',

    21â†’## ğŸ¯ Observer Path: Core GraphRAG Concepts
    22â†’
    23â†’In Sessions 1-5, you built sophisticated vector-based RAG systems with intelligent chunking, optimized search, query enhancement, and comprehensive evaluation. But when users ask complex questions like "What technologies do companies that partner with Apple use in automotive manufacturing?", you discover vector RAG's fundamental limitation: it finds similar content, but can't reason about relationships between entities.  
    24â†’
    25â†’This session transforms your RAG system from similarity matching to knowledge reasoning. You'll build graph-based architectures that capture entities, relationships, and hierarchical knowledge structures, enabling multi-hop reasoning that connects disparate information through logical pathways. The goal is moving from "find similar documents" to "understand and traverse knowledge relationships."  
    26â†’
    27â†’![RAG Architecture Overview](images/RAG-overview.png)
    28â†’
    29â†’### The Core GraphRAG Insight  
    30â†’
    31â†’Knowledge isn't just about content similarity â€“ it's about the relationships between concepts, entities, and facts. A question about Apple's automotive partnerships requires understanding:  
    32â†’
    33â†’1. Who Apple partners with  
    34â†’2. Which of those partners work in automotive  
    35â†’3. What technologies those automotive partners use  
    36â†’
    37â†’Vector RAG can find documents about each piece, but can't connect them logically. GraphRAG solves this by representing knowledge as a graph where nodes are entities/concepts and edges are relationships, enabling traversal through logical reasoning pathways.  
    38â†’
    39â†’## NodeRAG Architecture
    40â†’
    41â†’NodeRAG uses specialized node types and heterogeneous graph structures to enable sophisticated multi-hop reasoning and coherent knowledge retrieval.
    42â†’
    43â†’---
    44â†’
    45â†’## Part 1: NodeRAG - Structured Brain Architecture
    46â†’
    47â†’The challenge with vector RAG is that it treats all content uniformly â€“ a company name gets the same representation type as a concept or relationship. But knowledge has inherent structure: entities have attributes, relationships have directionality, and concepts have hierarchies. NodeRAG addresses this by creating specialized node types that preserve the semantic structure of different knowledge components.
    48â†’
    49â†’This isn't just theoretical improvement â€“ it enables reasoning capabilities that are impossible with flat vector representations.
    50â†’
    51â†’```
    52â†’Traditional RAG: Document â†’ Chunks â†’ Uniform Embeddings â†’ Similarity Search
    53â†’NodeRAG: Document â†’ Specialized Nodes â†’ Heterogeneous Graph â†’ Reasoning Pathways
    54â†’```
    55â†’
    56â†’### NodeRAG Key Features
    57â†’
    58â†’1. **Specialized Node Types**: Six distinct node types for different knowledge structures
    59â†’2. **Three-Stage Processing**: Decomposition â†’ Augmentation â†’ Enrichment
    60â†’3. **Personalized PageRank**: Semantic traversal following knowledge relationships
    61â†’4. **HNSW Integration**: Similarity edges within graph structure
    62â†’5. **Reasoning Pathways**: Multi-hop logical reasoning capabilities
    63â†’
    64â†’### NodeRAG's Six Specialized Node Types
    65â†’
    66â†’1. **Semantic Unit Nodes** - Abstract concepts and themes
    67â†’   - Example: "Supply Chain Management" connecting related methodologies

   400â†’## Bridge to Session 7: Agentic Reasoning
   401â†’
   402â†’NodeRAG's heterogeneous graph architecture provides the structured foundation for advanced reasoning capabilities. Session 7 will show how to build agents that actively reason through these graph structures.
   403â†’
   404â†’---
   405â†’
   406â†’## Part 2: Traditional GraphRAG Implementation - Building the Foundation
   407â†’
   408â†’### Knowledge Graph Construction from Documents
   409â†’
   410â†’Before implementing advanced NodeRAG architectures, it's essential to understand traditional GraphRAG approaches. Think of traditional GraphRAG as the foundation upon which more sophisticated graph reasoning is built. While NodeRAG provides specialized node types for complex reasoning, traditional GraphRAG establishes the core entity-relationship extraction and graph construction techniques that power all graph-based knowledge systems.
   411â†’
   412â†’Understanding both approaches gives you the flexibility to choose the right level of complexity for your specific use case.
   413â†’
   414â†’### Traditional GraphRAG: Foundational Entity-Relationship Extraction
   415â†’
   416â†’While NodeRAG provides advanced heterogeneous architectures, traditional GraphRAG remains valuable for:
   417â†’
   418â†’- **Simpler Use Cases**: When specialized node types aren't needed
   419â†’- **Resource Constraints**: Lower computational requirements
   420â†’- **Rapid Prototyping**: Faster implementation and iteration
   421â†’- **Legacy Integration**: Working with existing graph systems
   422â†’
   423â†’### Core Traditional GraphRAG Components
   424â†’
   425â†’1. **Entity Extraction**: Identify people, organizations, locations, concepts
   426â†’2. **Relationship Mapping**: Connect entities through typed relationships
   427â†’3. **Graph Construction**: Build searchable knowledge graph
   428â†’4. **Query Processing**: Traverse graph for multi-hop reasoning
   429â†’
   430â†’```python
   431â†’
   432â†’# NodeRAG: Heterogeneous Graph Architecture for Advanced Knowledge Representation
   433â†’
   434â†’import spacy
   435â†’from typing import List, Dict, Any, Tuple, Set, Union
   436â†’import networkx as nx

  2675â†’Hybrid response generation combines information from both vector similarity and graph traversal searches into coherent, comprehensive answers.   2676â†’
  2677â†’```python
  2678â†’        # Construct dual-context prompt for comprehensive reasoning
  2679â†’        response_prompt = f"""
  2680â†’        You are an expert analyst with access to both direct factual information and relationship knowledge.
  2681â†’        
  2682â†’        Question: {query}
  2683â†’        
  2684â†’        DIRECT FACTUAL INFORMATION:
  2685â†’        {self._format_vector_contexts(vector_contexts)}
  2686â†’        
  2687â†’        RELATIONSHIP KNOWLEDGE:
  2688â†’        {self._format_graph_contexts(graph_contexts)}
  2689â†’

  2691â†’        1. Provide a comprehensive answer using both types of information
  2692â†’        2. When using relationship knowledge, explain the connections clearly
  2693â†’        3. Cite sources appropriately, distinguishing between direct facts and inferred relationships
  2694â†’        4. If graph relationships reveal additional insights, highlight them
  2695â†’        5. Maintain accuracy and avoid making unsupported claims
  2696â†’        
  2697â†’        Provide a well-structured response that leverages both factual and relationship information:
  2698â†’        """
  2699â†’```
  2700â†’
  2701â†’The hybrid prompt template explicitly distinguishes between factual information (from vector search) and relationship knowledge (from graph traversal). This distinction enables the LLM to appropriately handle each information type - treating direct facts as authoritative while explaining relationship-based insights as inferences. The instruction set guides the model to synthesize both types of information while maintaining proper attribution and confidence levels.

   227â†’## Learning Outcomes
   228â†’
   229â†’Upon completion of this module, you will master:
   230â†’
   231â†’### RAG System Design
   232â†’
   233â†’- Architect comprehensive RAG systems from requirements to deployment
   234â†’- Select optimal components for specific use cases and constraints
   235â†’- Design scalable, maintainable RAG architectures
   236â†’
   237â†’### Advanced Implementation
   238â†’
   239â†’- Implement sophisticated retrieval strategies and query optimization
   240â†’- Build multi-modal RAG systems handling diverse content types
   241â†’- Create agentic RAG systems with self-improvement capabilities
   242â†’
   243â†’### Production Excellence
   244â†’
   245â†’- Deploy enterprise-grade RAG systems with proper security and compliance
   246â†’- Implement comprehensive monitoring, evaluation, and optimization workflows
   247â†’- Integrate RAG systems into existing enterprise infrastructure
   248â†’
   249â†’### Quality & Evaluation
   250â†’
   251â†’- Design and implement robust evaluation frameworks
   252â†’- Monitor and improve system performance continuously
   253â†’- Balance accuracy, latency, and cost considerations
   254â†’

ğŸ“‹ Detailed report saved to: code-block-analysis.json
   215â†’Graph construction creates nodes for entities and edges for relationships, forming the queryable knowledge structure.
   216â†’
   217â†’#### Query Processing and Graph Traversal
   218â†’
   219â†’```python
   220â†’    def query_graph(self, query: str, max_hops: int = 3):
   221â†’        """Query the knowledge graph for relevant information"""
   222â†’        
   223â†’        # Extract entities from query
   224â†’        query_doc = self.nlp(query)
   225â†’        query_entities = [ent.text for ent in query_doc.ents]
   226â†’        
   227â†’        # Find paths between query entities
   228â†’        relevant_paths = []
   229â†’        
   230â†’        for i, entity1 in enumerate(query_entities):
   231â†’            for entity2 in query_entities[i+1:]:
   232â†’                if (self.graph.has_node(entity1) and 
   233â†’                    self.graph.has_node(entity2)):
   234â†’                    try:
   235â†’                        path = nx.shortest_path(
   236â†’                            self.graph, entity1, entity2
   237â†’                        )
   238â†’                        if len(path) <= max_hops + 1:
   239â†’                            relevant_paths.append(path)
   240â†’                    except nx.NetworkXNoPath:
   241â†’                        continue
   242â†’        
   243â†’        return relevant_paths
   244â†’```
   245â†’
   246â†’Query processing finds paths between entities mentioned in the query, enabling multi-hop reasoning.
   247â†’
   248â†’### Code GraphRAG Implementation - Understanding Software Knowledge
   249â†’

  2311â†’**Security Checklist**:
  2312â†’- [ ] All API endpoints require authentication
  2313â†’- [ ] Sensitive data is encrypted at rest
  2314â†’- [ ] All data access is logged for audit
  2315â†’- [ ] Users have minimal necessary permissions
  2316â†’- [ ] Secrets are managed securely (not in code)
  2317â†’- [ ] Rate limiting prevents abuse
  2318â†’

  2440â†’
  2441â†’16. **Which metric type is most appropriate for tracking the number of API requests?**
  2442â†’    a) Gauge
  2443â†’    b) Counter
  2444â†’    c) Histogram
  2445â†’    d) Summary
  2446â†’
  2447â†’17. **What is the primary benefit of distributed tracing in multi-agent systems?**
  2448â†’    a) Reduced latency
  2449â†’    b) Understanding request flow across multiple services
  2450â†’    c) Lower memory usage
  2451â†’    d) Improved security
  2452â†’
  2453â†’18. **How do SLA violations typically trigger automated responses?**
  2454â†’    a) Manual intervention only
  2455â†’    b) Through alert rules and escalation policies
  2456â†’    c) System restart
  2457â†’    d) Data backup
  2458â†’
  2459â†’19. **What factors should influence auto-scaling decisions in enterprise environments?**
  2460â†’    a) CPU utilization only
  2461â†’    b) Multiple metrics including CPU, memory, queue length, and response time
  2462â†’    c) Time of day only
  2463â†’    d) Random intervals
  2464â†’
  2465â†’20. **Which caching strategy provides the best performance for frequently accessed data?**
  2466â†’    a) No caching
  2467â†’    b) Multi-level caching with intelligent eviction policies
  2468â†’    c) Single-level caching only
  2469â†’    d) Database-only storage
  2470â†’
  2471â†’---
  2472â†’
  2473â†’## Answer Key
  2474â†’
  2475â†’1. **c)** Fault isolation and preventing cascade failures - Circuit breakers prevent failures from propagating through the system
  2476â†’2. **c)** Multi-factor authentication with certificate-based auth - Provides the highest security level
  2477â†’3. **b)** Traffic management, security, and observability - Service mesh provides comprehensive communication control
  2478â†’4. **b)** By providing fine-grained permissions based on user roles - RBAC ensures users have appropriate access levels
  2479â†’5. **b)** Smaller final image size and improved security - Multi-stage builds separate build and runtime dependencies
  2480â†’6. **d)** Both b and c are correct - Both rolling updates and blue-green deployments can achieve zero downtime
  2481â†’7. **b)** Automatic failure detection and recovery - Health probes enable Kubernetes to automatically manage container health
  2482â†’8. **c)** Integrated security scanning and vulnerability assessment - Security must be integrated throughout the pipeline
  2483â†’9. **b)** Parameterized and reusable deployment templates - Helm enables consistent deployments across environments
  2484â†’10. **c)** Both a and b are correct - Different probe types serve different purposes
  2485â†’11. **b)** Valid consent and lawful basis for processing personal data - GDPR requires explicit consent and legal justification
  2486â†’12. **b)** Asymmetric encryption with key rotation - Provides strong security with manageable key lifecycle
  2487â†’13. **b)** Applying appropriate security controls based on data sensitivity - Classification drives security policy application
  2488â†’14. **b)** Users get only minimum permissions needed for their role - Minimizes potential security exposure
  2489â†’15. **b)** Providing evidence of compliance and supporting incident investigation - Audit logs are essential for compliance proof
  2490â†’16. **b)** Counter - Counters are designed for monotonically increasing values like request counts
  2491â†’17. **b)** Understanding request flow across multiple services - Distributed tracing provides end-to-end visibility
  2492â†’18. **b)** Through alert rules and escalation policies - Automated response systems handle SLA violations consistently
  2493â†’19. **b)** Multiple metrics including CPU, memory, queue length, and response time - Comprehensive metrics provide better scaling decisions
  2494â†’20. **b)** Multi-level caching with intelligent eviction policies - Provides optimal performance with efficient resource usage
  2495â†’
  2496â†’---
  2497â†’

  2502â†’3. **Security & Compliance** demands comprehensive authentication, authorization, encryption, and regulatory compliance

     1â†’# Session 0: Introduction to Agent Frameworks & Patterns - Test Solutions
     2â†’
     3â†’## ğŸ“ Multiple Choice Test
     4â†’
     5â†’### Question 1: Agentic Patterns
     6â†’**Which agentic pattern involves an agent evaluating and improving its own outputs?**
     7â†’
     8â†’A) Tool Use  
     9â†’B) Reflection âœ…  
    10â†’C) Planning  
    11â†’D) Multi-Agent  
    12â†’
    13â†’**Explanation:** The reflection pattern specifically involves agents evaluating and improving their own outputs through iterative self-assessment. This pattern includes generating initial output, reflecting on quality, and refining based on critique.
    14â†’
    15â†’---
    16â†’
    17â†’### Question 2: ReAct Pattern
    18â†’**The ReAct pattern combines which two key capabilities?**
    19â†’
    20â†’A) Reading and Acting  
    21â†’B) Reasoning and Acting âœ…  
    22â†’C) Reflecting and Acting  
    23â†’D) Retrieving and Acting  
    24â†’
    25â†’**Explanation:** ReAct stands for Reasoning and Acting, combining these capabilities in iterative loops. The agent reasons about what to do next, takes action, observes results, and continues the reasoning-action cycle.
    26â†’
    27â†’---
    28â†’
    29â†’### Question 3: Performance-Optimized Framework
    30â†’**Which framework is best suited for high-performance applications with minimal resource usage?**
    31â†’
    32â†’A) LangChain  
    33â†’B) CrewAI  
    34â†’C) Agno âœ…  
    35â†’D) PydanticAI  
    36â†’
    37â†’**Explanation:** Agno is optimized for performance with claims of 50x more memory efficiency and 10,000x faster agent instantiation, making it ideal for high-performance applications.
    38â†’
    39â†’---
    40â†’
    41â†’### Question 4: Multi-Agent Advantage
    42â†’**What is the primary advantage of the Multi-Agent pattern?**
    43â†’
    44â†’A) Faster execution  
    45â†’B) Specialized expertise collaboration âœ…  
    46â†’C) Reduced complexity  
    47â†’D) Lower resource usage  
    48â†’
    49â†’**Explanation:** Multi-Agent patterns allow different agents with specialized skills to collaborate on complex problems, leveraging the expertise of each agent for optimal results.
    50â†’

8. **b) LangGraph** - LangGraph extends LangChain with graph-based architecture using nodes and edges for precise control flow.

9. **c) Pre-built components and patterns** - Frameworks provide tested implementations of common patterns, reducing development time and complexity.

10. **b) Parallel Processing** - Parallel processing involves multiple agents working simultaneously on different aspects of a problem.

11. **b) Learning fundamentals and custom research** - Bare metal implementation provides complete control and understanding of underlying mechanisms.

12. **b) 3 phases: Generate, Reflect, Refine** - The core reflection pattern involves generating initial output, reflecting on quality, then refining based on critique.

13. **b) Built-in security, monitoring, and Google Cloud integration** - ADK provides enterprise features like security, compliance, monitoring, and cloud-native integration.

14. **c) Coordinate worker agents and manage interactions** - Manager agents orchestrate team activities and handle inter-agent communication.

15. **b) Tool Use (for accessing live data APIs)** - Real-time stock analysis requires accessing external APIs for current market data, making Tool Use the most appropriate pattern.

  1071â†’                text=f"Contents of {path}:\n\n{content}"
  1072â†’            )]
  1073â†’            
  1074â†’        except Exception as e:
  1075â†’            logger.error(f"Error reading file {path}: {e}")
  1076â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1077â†’                type="text",
  1078â†’                text=f"Error reading file: {str(e)}"
  1079â†’            )]
  1080â†’    
  1081â†’    elif name == "list_directory":
  1082â†’        path = Path(arguments["path"])
  1083â†’        
  1084â†’        # Security validation
  1085â†’        if not is_safe_path(path, ALLOWED_DIRS):
  1086â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1087â†’                type="text",
  1088â†’                text=f"Error: Access denied. Path {path} is outside allowed directories."
  1089â†’            )]
  1090â†’        
  1091â†’        try:
  1092â†’            if not path.exists():
  1093â†’                return [types.TextContent(
  1094â†’                    type="text",
  1095â†’                    text=f"Error: Directory {path} does not exist."
  1096â†’                )]
  1097â†’            
  1098â†’            if not path.is_dir():
  1099â†’                return [types.TextContent(
  1100â†’                    type="text",
  1101â†’                    text=f"Error: {path} is not a directory. Use read_file for files."
  1102â†’                )]
  1103â†’            
  1104â†’            # List directory contents with useful information
  1105â†’            items = []
  1106â†’            for item in sorted(path.iterdir()):
  1107â†’                if item.is_dir():
  1108â†’                    items.append(f"ğŸ“ {item.name}/")
  1109â†’                else:
  1110â†’                    size = item.stat().st_size
  1111â†’                    items.append(f"ğŸ“„ {item.name} ({size} bytes)")
  1112â†’            
  1113â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1114â†’                type="text",
  1115â†’                text=f"Contents of {path}:\n\n" + "\n".join(items)
  1116â†’            )]
  1117â†’            
  1118â†’        except Exception as e:
  1119â†’            logger.error(f"Error listing directory {path}: {e}")
  1120â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1121â†’                type="text",
  1122â†’                text=f"Error listing directory: {str(e)}"
  1123â†’            )]
  1124â†’    
  1125â†’    elif name == "get_file_info":
  1126â†’        path = Path(arguments["path"])
  1127â†’        
  1128â†’        # Security validation
  1129â†’        if not is_safe_path(path, ALLOWED_DIRS):
  1130â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1131â†’                type="text",
  1132â†’                text=f"Error: Access denied. Path {path} is outside allowed directories."
  1133â†’            )]
  1134â†’        
  1135â†’        try:
  1136â†’            if not path.exists():
  1137â†’                return [types.TextContent(
  1138â†’                    type="text",
  1139â†’                    text=f"Error: Path {path} does not exist."
  1140â†’                )]
  1141â†’            
  1142â†’            stat = path.stat()
  1143â†’            mime_type, _ = mimetypes.guess_type(str(path))
  1144â†’            
  1145â†’            info_lines = [
  1146â†’                f"Path: {path}",
  1147â†’                f"Type: {'Directory' if path.is_dir() else 'File'}",
  1148â†’                f"Size: {stat.st_size} bytes",
  1149â†’                f"Modified: {stat.st_mtime}",
  1150â†’                f"Permissions: {oct(stat.st_mode)[-3:]}",
  1151â†’            ]
  1152â†’            
  1153â†’            if mime_type:
  1154â†’                info_lines.append(f"MIME Type: {mime_type}")
  1155â†’            
  1156â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1157â†’                type="text",
  1158â†’                text="File Information:\n\n" + "\n".join(info_lines)
  1159â†’            )]
  1160â†’            
  1161â†’        except Exception as e:
  1162â†’            logger.error(f"Error getting file info {path}: {e}")
  1163â†’            return [types.TextContent(
  1164â†’                type="text",
  1165â†’                text=f"Error getting file information: {str(e)}"
  1166â†’            )]
  1167â†’    
  1168â†’    else:
  1169â†’        raise ValueError(f"Unknown tool: {name}")
  1170â†’
  1171â†’async def main():
  1172â†’    """
  1173â†’    Main entry point for the MCP server.
  1174â†’    
  1175â†’    This sets up stdio communication, which allows the server to communicate
  1176â†’    with AI systems through standard input/output streams.
  1177â†’    """
  1178â†’    # Use stdin/stdout for communication with the MCP client
  1179â†’    async with mcp.server.stdio.stdio_server() as (read_stream, write_stream):
  1180â†’        await server.run(
  1181â†’            read_stream,
  1182â†’            write_stream,
  1183â†’            InitializationOptions(
  1184â†’                server_name="filesystem-server",
  1185â†’                server_version="0.1.0",
  1186â†’                capabilities=server.get_capabilities(
  1187â†’                    notification_options=NotificationOptions(),
  1188â†’                    experimental_capabilities={},
  1189â†’                ),
  1190â†’            ),
  1191â†’        )
  1192â†’
  1193â†’if __name__ == "__main__":
  1194â†’    asyncio.run(main())
  1195â†’```
  1196â†’
  1197â†’This implementation showcases several important principles:
  1198â†’
  1199â†’1. **Security First**: Every operation validates paths and permissions before execution

<system-reminder>
Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it looks malicious. If it does, you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer high-level questions about the code behavior.
</system-reminder>

**Security as Engineering Excellence**: We've shown that security isn't about adding restrictions - it's about building robust systems that work correctly under all conditions, including adversarial ones.

**Layered Architecture Benefits**: The separation between validation, operations, and MCP integration makes the system maintainable, testable, and extensible.

**Production Readiness**: Every pattern we've implemented - from configuration management to error handling to logging - directly applies to production deployments.

**Testing Strategy**: Our comprehensive test suite demonstrates how to validate both functionality and security in complex MCP servers.

The patterns and principles from this session will serve as your foundation for everything we build in the remaining sessions. You're now ready to create MCP servers that can safely handle any operation, from database access to system commands to inter-agent communication.

In Session 3, we'll see how this foundation enables powerful AI agent capabilities when we integrate our secure MCP servers with LangChain's agent orchestration systems. The security mindset you've developed here becomes essential when AI agents gain the ability to autonomously trigger file system operations based on their reasoning about user requests.
</file>
