     1â†’# Session 3 - Module A: Enterprise Agent Patterns
     2â†’
     3â†’> **ADVANCED OPTIONAL MODULE** - Complete Session 3 core content first.
     4â†’
     5â†’Enterprise MCP agent deployments require sophisticated patterns for production reliability, including circuit breakers, connection pooling, security controls, and comprehensive monitoring.
     6â†’
     7â†’## Advanced Production Patterns
     8â†’
     9â†’### Pattern 1: Circuit Breaker for MCP Server Resilience
    10â†’
    11â†’Enterprise agents must handle partial system failures gracefully. The circuit breaker pattern prevents cascading failures when MCP servers become unavailable.
    12â†’
    13â†’```python
    14â†’# utils/circuit_breaker.py
    15â†’import asyncio
    16â†’import time
    17â†’from enum import Enum
    18â†’from typing import Dict, Any, Callable, Optional
    19â†’from dataclasses import dataclass
    20â†’import logging
    21â†’
    22â†’logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
    23â†’
    24â†’class CircuitState(Enum):
    25â†’    CLOSED = "closed"      # Normal operation
    26â†’    OPEN = "open"          # Failure state - reject requests
    27â†’    HALF_OPEN = "half_open" # Testing if service recovered
    28â†’
    29â†’@dataclass
    30â†’class CircuitBreakerConfig:
    31â†’    failure_threshold: int = 5      # Failures before opening
    32â†’    recovery_timeout: int = 60      # Seconds before trying again
    33â†’    success_threshold: int = 3      # Successes needed to close
    34â†’    timeout: int = 30              # Request timeout
    35â†’
    36â†’class CircuitBreaker:
    37â†’    """Circuit breaker for MCP server calls with enterprise reliability."""
    38â†’    
    39â†’    def __init__(self, name: str, config: CircuitBreakerConfig):
    40â†’        self.name = name
    41â†’        self.config = config
    42â†’        self.state = CircuitState.CLOSED
    43â†’        self.failure_count = 0
    44â†’        self.success_count = 0
    45â†’        self.last_failure_time = 0
    46â†’        self.metrics = {
    47â†’            "total_requests": 0,
    48â†’            "successful_requests": 0,
    49â†’            "failed_requests": 0,
    50â†’            "circuit_opens": 0
    51â†’        }
    52â†’    
    53â†’    async def call(self, func: Callable, *args, **kwargs) -> Any:
    54â†’        """Execute function with circuit breaker protection."""
    55â†’        self.metrics["total_requests"] += 1
    56â†’        
    57â†’        if self.state == CircuitState.OPEN:
    58â†’            if time.time() - self.last_failure_time > self.config.recovery_timeout:
    59â†’                self.state = CircuitState.HALF_OPEN
    60â†’                self.success_count = 0
    61â†’                logger.info(f"Circuit breaker {self.name} entering HALF_OPEN state")
    62â†’            else:
    63â†’                raise CircuitBreakerOpenError(f"Circuit breaker {self.name} is OPEN")
    64â†’        
    65â†’        try:
    66â†’            # Execute with timeout
    67â†’            result = await asyncio.wait_for(
    68â†’                func(*args, **kwargs),
    69â†’                timeout=self.config.timeout
    70â†’            )
    71â†’            
    72â†’            await self._on_success()
    73â†’            return result
    74â†’            
    75â†’        except Exception as e:
    76â†’            await self._on_failure()
    77â†’            raise e
    78â†’    
    79â†’    async def _on_success(self):
    80â†’        """Handle successful operation."""
    81â†’        self.metrics["successful_requests"] += 1
    82â†’        
    83â†’        if self.state == CircuitState.HALF_OPEN:
    84â†’            self.success_count += 1
    85â†’            if self.success_count >= self.config.success_threshold:
    86â†’                self.state = CircuitState.CLOSED
    87â†’                self.failure_count = 0
    88â†’                logger.info(f"Circuit breaker {self.name} CLOSED - service recovered")
    89â†’        else:
    90â†’            self.failure_count = 0  # Reset failure count on success
    91â†’    
    92â†’    async def _on_failure(self):
    93â†’        """Handle failed operation."""
    94â†’        self.metrics["failed_requests"] += 1
    95â†’        self.failure_count += 1
    96â†’        self.last_failure_time = time.time()
    97â†’        
    98â†’        if (self.state == CircuitState.CLOSED and 
    99â†’            self.failure_count >= self.config.failure_threshold):
   100â†’            self.state = CircuitState.OPEN
   101â†’            self.metrics["circuit_opens"] += 1
   102â†’            logger.error(f"Circuit breaker {self.name} OPENED - service failing")
   103â†’        
   104â†’        elif self.state == CircuitState.HALF_OPEN:
   105â†’            self.state = CircuitState.OPEN
   106â†’            logger.warning(f"Circuit breaker {self.name} back to OPEN - service still failing")
   107â†’
   108â†’class CircuitBreakerOpenError(Exception):
   109â†’    """Raised when circuit breaker is open."""
   110â†’    pass
   111â†’```
   112â†’
   113â†’### Pattern 2: Enhanced MCP Manager with Connection Pooling
   114â†’
   115â†’Production deployments require efficient resource management and connection pooling to handle high concurrency.
   116â†’
   117â†’```python
   118â†’# utils/enterprise_mcp_manager.py
   119â†’import asyncio
   120â†’import time
   121â†’from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Any
   122â†’from contextlib import asynccontextmanager
   123â†’from langchain_mcp_adapters import MCPAdapter
   124â†’from config import Config, MCPServerConfig
   125â†’from .circuit_breaker import CircuitBreaker, CircuitBreakerConfig
   126â†’
   127â†’logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
   128â†’
   129â†’class ConnectionPool:
   130â†’    """Manages a pool of MCP adapter connections for high concurrency."""
   131â†’    
   132â†’    def __init__(self, server_config: MCPServerConfig, pool_size: int = 5):
   133â†’        self.server_config = server_config
   134â†’        self.pool_size = pool_size
   135â†’        self.available_connections: asyncio.Queue = asyncio.Queue(maxsize=pool_size)
   136â†’        self.total_connections = 0
   137â†’        self.metrics = {
   138â†’            "connections_created": 0,
   139â†’            "connections_reused": 0,
   140â†’            "pool_exhausted_count": 0
   141â†’        }
   142â†’    
   143â†’    async def initialize(self):
   144â†’        """Pre-populate connection pool."""
   145â†’        for _ in range(self.pool_size):
   146â†’            adapter = await self._create_connection()
   147â†’            if adapter:
   148â†’                await self.available_connections.put(adapter)
   149â†’    
   150â†’    async def _create_connection(self) -> Optional[MCPAdapter]:
   151â†’        """Create a new MCP adapter connection."""
   152â†’        try:
   153â†’            adapter = MCPAdapter(
   154â†’                command=self.server_config.command,
   155â†’                args=self.server_config.args,
   156â†’                timeout=self.server_config.timeout
   157â†’            )
   158â†’            await adapter.start()
   159â†’            self.total_connections += 1
   160â†’            self.metrics["connections_created"] += 1
   161â†’            return adapter
   162â†’        except Exception as e:
   163â†’            logger.error(f"Failed to create connection for {self.server_config.name}: {e}")
   164â†’            return None
   165â†’    
   166â†’    @asynccontextmanager
   167â†’    async def get_connection(self):
   168â†’        """Get connection from pool with automatic return."""
   169â†’        adapter = None
   170â†’        try:
   171â†’            # Try to get existing connection
   172â†’            try:
   173â†’                adapter = self.available_connections.get_nowait()
   174â†’                self.metrics["connections_reused"] += 1
   175â†’            except asyncio.QueueEmpty:
   176â†’                # Pool exhausted, create new connection
   177â†’                self.metrics["pool_exhausted_count"] += 1
   178â†’                adapter = await self._create_connection()
   179â†’                if not adapter:
   180â†’                    raise ConnectionError(f"Failed to create connection for {self.server_config.name}")
   181â†’            
   182â†’            yield adapter
   183â†’            
   184â†’        finally:
   185â†’            # Return connection to pool if still valid
   186â†’            if adapter:
   187â†’                try:
   188â†’                    self.available_connections.put_nowait(adapter)
   189â†’                except asyncio.QueueFull:
   190â†’                    # Pool full, close excess connection
   191â†’                    await adapter.stop()
   192â†’                    self.total_connections -= 1
   193â†’
   194â†’class EnterpriseMCPManager:
   195â†’    """Production-grade MCP server manager with advanced patterns."""
   196â†’    
   197â†’    def __init__(self, server_configs: List[MCPServerConfig]):
   198â†’        self.server_configs = {config.name: config for config in server_configs}
   199â†’        self.connection_pools: Dict[str, ConnectionPool] = {}
   200â†’        self.circuit_breakers: Dict[str, CircuitBreaker] = {}
   201â†’        self.health_status: Dict[str, bool] = {}
   202â†’        self.metrics = {
   203â†’            "total_requests": 0,
   204â†’            "successful_requests": 0,
   205â†’            "failed_requests": 0,
   206â†’            "average_response_time": 0.0
   207â†’        }
   208â†’        self._monitoring_task: Optional[asyncio.Task] = None
   209â†’    
   210â†’    async def initialize(self):
   211â†’        """Initialize all connection pools and circuit breakers."""
   212â†’        for name, config in self.server_configs.items():
   213â†’            # Create connection pool
   214â†’            pool = ConnectionPool(config, pool_size=5)
   215â†’            await pool.initialize()
   216â†’            self.connection_pools[name] = pool
   217â†’            
   218â†’            # Create circuit breaker
   219â†’            cb_config = CircuitBreakerConfig(
   220â†’                failure_threshold=5,
   221â†’                recovery_timeout=60,
   222â†’                success_threshold=3,
   223â†’                timeout=config.timeout
   224â†’            )
   225â†’            self.circuit_breakers[name] = CircuitBreaker(name, cb_config)
   226â†’            
   227â†’            self.health_status[name] = True
   228â†’            logger.info(f"Initialized enterprise MCP manager for {name}")
   229â†’        
   230â†’        # Start monitoring task
   231â†’        self._monitoring_task = asyncio.create_task(self._monitoring_loop())
   232â†’    
   233â†’    async def call_tool(self, server_name: str, tool_name: str, args: Dict[str, Any]) -> Any:
   234â†’        """Call tool with enterprise patterns: pooling, circuit breaker, metrics."""
   235â†’        start_time = time.time()
   236â†’        self.metrics["total_requests"] += 1
   237â†’        
   238â†’        if server_name not in self.connection_pools:
   239â†’            raise ValueError(f"Server {server_name} not configured")
   240â†’        
   241â†’        pool = self.connection_pools[server_name]
   242â†’        circuit_breaker = self.circuit_breakers[server_name]
   243â†’        
   244â†’        try:
   245â†’            async def _call_with_pool():
   246â†’                async with pool.get_connection() as adapter:
   247â†’                    return await adapter.call_tool(tool_name, args)
   248â†’            
   249â†’            # Execute with circuit breaker protection
   250â†’            result = await circuit_breaker.call(_call_with_pool)
   251â†’            
   252â†’            # Update metrics
   253â†’            response_time = time.time() - start_time
   254â†’            self.metrics["successful_requests"] += 1
   255â†’            self._update_average_response_time(response_time)
   256â†’            
   257â†’            return result
   258â†’            
   259â†’        except Exception as e:
   260â†’            self.metrics["failed_requests"] += 1
   261â†’            self.health_status[server_name] = False
   262â†’            logger.error(f"Tool call failed for {server_name}.{tool_name}: {e}")
   263â†’            raise
   264â†’    
   265â†’    def _update_average_response_time(self, response_time: float):
   266â†’        """Update rolling average response time."""
   267â†’        current_avg = self.metrics["average_response_time"]
   268â†’        total_requests = self.metrics["successful_requests"]
   269â†’        
   270â†’        # Calculate rolling average
   271â†’        self.metrics["average_response_time"] = (
   272â†’            (current_avg * (total_requests - 1) + response_time) / total_requests
   273â†’        )
   274â†’    
   275â†’    async def _monitoring_loop(self):
   276â†’        """Continuous monitoring and health checks."""
   277â†’        while True:
   278â†’            try:
   279â†’                for name in self.server_configs.keys():
   280â†’                    await self._health_check(name)
   281â†’                await asyncio.sleep(30)  # Check every 30 seconds
   282â†’            except asyncio.CancelledError:
   283â†’                break
   284â†’            except Exception as e:
   285â†’                logger.error(f"Monitoring loop error: {e}")
   286â†’                await asyncio.sleep(5)
   287â†’    
   288â†’    async def _health_check(self, server_name: str):
   289â†’        """Perform health check on server."""
   290â†’        try:
   291â†’            # Simple health check by listing tools
   292â†’            pool = self.connection_pools[server_name]
   293â†’            async with pool.get_connection() as adapter:
   294â†’                await adapter.list_tools()
   295â†’            
   296â†’            self.health_status[server_name] = True
   297â†’            
   298â†’        except Exception as e:
   299â†’            self.health_status[server_name] = False
   300â†’            logger.warning(f"Health check failed for {server_name}: {e}")
   301â†’    
   302â†’    def get_metrics(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
   303â†’        """Get comprehensive metrics for monitoring."""
   304â†’        server_metrics = {}
   305â†’        for name, cb in self.circuit_breakers.items():
   306â†’            server_metrics[name] = {
   307â†’                "circuit_breaker_state": cb.state.value,
   308â†’                "circuit_breaker_metrics": cb.metrics,
   309â†’                "connection_pool_metrics": self.connection_pools[name].metrics,
   310â†’                "health_status": self.health_status[name]
   311â†’            }
   312â†’        
   313â†’        return {
   314â†’            "global_metrics": self.metrics,
   315â†’            "server_metrics": server_metrics
   316â†’        }
   317â†’    
   318â†’    async def cleanup(self):
   319â†’        """Clean up resources."""
   320â†’        if self._monitoring_task:
   321â†’            self._monitoring_task.cancel()
   322â†’            try:
   323â†’                await self._monitoring_task
   324â†’            except asyncio.CancelledError:
   325â†’                pass
   326â†’        
   327â†’        # Close all connections
   328â†’        for pool in self.connection_pools.values():
   329â†’            while pool.total_connections > 0:
   330â†’                try:
   331â†’                    adapter = pool.available_connections.get_nowait()
   332â†’                    await adapter.stop()
   333â†’                    pool.total_connections -= 1
   334â†’                except asyncio.QueueEmpty:
   335â†’                    break
   336â†’```
   337â†’
   338â†’### Pattern 3: Enterprise Security and Access Control
   339â†’
   340â†’Production agents require sophisticated access control and audit logging.
   341â†’
   342â†’```python
   343â†’# security/enterprise_auth.py
   344â†’import jwt
   345â†’import time
   346â†’from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Set
   347â†’from dataclasses import dataclass
   348â†’from enum import Enum
   349â†’import logging
   350â†’
   351â†’logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
   352â†’
   353â†’class Permission(Enum):
   354â†’    READ_WEATHER = "weather:read"
   355â†’    READ_FILES = "files:read"
   356â†’    WRITE_FILES = "files:write"
   357â†’    QUERY_DATABASE = "database:query"
   358â†’    MODIFY_DATABASE = "database:modify"
   359â†’    ADMIN_TOOLS = "admin:*"
   360â†’
   361â†’@dataclass
   362â†’class UserContext:
   363â†’    user_id: str
   364â†’    roles: Set[str]
   365â†’    permissions: Set[Permission]
   366â†’    session_id: str
   367â†’    expires_at: float
   368â†’    organization_id: str
   369â†’
   370â†’class EnterpriseAuthenticator:
   371â†’    """Enterprise authentication and authorization for MCP agents."""
   372â†’    
   373â†’    def __init__(self, jwt_secret: str, default_permissions: Dict[str, List[Permission]]):
   374â†’        self.jwt_secret = jwt_secret
   375â†’        self.default_permissions = default_permissions
   376â†’        self.active_sessions: Dict[str, UserContext] = {}
   377â†’        self.audit_log: List[Dict] = []
   378â†’    
   379â†’    def authenticate_token(self, token: str) -> Optional[UserContext]:
   380â†’        """Authenticate JWT token and return user context."""
   381â†’        try:
   382â†’            payload = jwt.decode(token, self.jwt_secret, algorithms=["HS256"])
   383â†’            
   384â†’            user_id = payload.get("user_id")
   385â†’            roles = set(payload.get("roles", []))
   386â†’            session_id = payload.get("session_id")
   387â†’            expires_at = payload.get("exp", 0)
   388â†’            organization_id = payload.get("org_id")
   389â†’            
   390â†’            if time.time() > expires_at:
   391â†’                self._audit("TOKEN_EXPIRED", {"user_id": user_id})
   392â†’                return None
   393â†’            
   394â†’            # Calculate permissions from roles
   395â†’            permissions = set()
   396â†’            for role in roles:
   397â†’                permissions.update(self.default_permissions.get(role, []))
   398â†’            
   399â†’            user_context = UserContext(
   400â†’                user_id=user_id,
   401â†’                roles=roles,
   402â†’                permissions=permissions,
   403â†’                session_id=session_id,
   404â†’                expires_at=expires_at,
   405â†’                organization_id=organization_id
   406â†’            )
   407â†’            
   408â†’            self.active_sessions[session_id] = user_context
   409â†’            self._audit("USER_AUTHENTICATED", {"user_id": user_id, "roles": list(roles)})
   410â†’            
   411â†’            return user_context
   412â†’            
   413â†’        except jwt.InvalidTokenError as e:
   414â†’            self._audit("INVALID_TOKEN", {"error": str(e)})
   415â†’            return None
   416â†’    
   417â†’    def authorize_tool_access(self, user_context: UserContext, server_name: str, tool_name: str) -> bool:
   418â†’        """Check if user has permission to access specific tool."""
   419â†’        required_permission = self._get_required_permission(server_name, tool_name)
   420â†’        
   421â†’        if required_permission in user_context.permissions:
   422â†’            self._audit("TOOL_ACCESS_GRANTED", {
   423â†’                "user_id": user_context.user_id,
   424â†’                "server": server_name,
   425â†’                "tool": tool_name
   426â†’            })
   427â†’            return True
   428â†’        
   429â†’        self._audit("TOOL_ACCESS_DENIED", {
   430â†’            "user_id": user_context.user_id,
   431â†’            "server": server_name,
   432â†’            "tool": tool_name,
   433â†’            "required_permission": required_permission.value
   434â†’        })
   435â†’        return False
   436â†’    
   437â†’    def _get_required_permission(self, server_name: str, tool_name: str) -> Permission:
   438â†’        """Map server/tool combinations to required permissions."""
   439â†’        permission_map = {
   440â†’            ("weather", "get_current_weather"): Permission.READ_WEATHER,
   441â†’            ("weather", "get_forecast"): Permission.READ_WEATHER,
   442â†’            ("filesystem", "read_file"): Permission.READ_FILES,
   443â†’            ("filesystem", "write_file"): Permission.WRITE_FILES,
   444â†’            ("filesystem", "list_files"): Permission.READ_FILES,
   445â†’            ("database", "query"): Permission.QUERY_DATABASE,
   446â†’            ("database", "insert"): Permission.MODIFY_DATABASE,
   447â†’            ("database", "update"): Permission.MODIFY_DATABASE,
   448â†’        }
   449â†’        
   450â†’        return permission_map.get((server_name, tool_name), Permission.ADMIN_TOOLS)
   451â†’    
   452â†’    def _audit(self, action: str, details: Dict):
   453â†’        """Log security events for audit trail."""
   454â†’        audit_entry = {
   455â†’            "timestamp": time.time(),
   456â†’            "action": action,
   457â†’            "details": details
   458â†’        }
   459â†’        
   460â†’        self.audit_log.append(audit_entry)
   461â†’        logger.info(f"SECURITY_AUDIT: {action} - {details}")
   462â†’        
   463â†’        # Keep only last 1000 entries in memory
   464â†’        if len(self.audit_log) > 1000:
   465â†’            self.audit_log = self.audit_log[-1000:]
   466â†’    
   467â†’    def get_audit_log(self, user_id: Optional[str] = None, limit: int = 100) -> List[Dict]:
   468â†’        """Retrieve audit log entries."""
   469â†’        if user_id:
   470â†’            filtered_log = [
   471â†’                entry for entry in self.audit_log 
   472â†’                if entry["details"].get("user_id") == user_id
   473â†’            ]
   474â†’        else:
   475â†’            filtered_log = self.audit_log
   476â†’        
   477â†’        return filtered_log[-limit:]
   478â†’```
   479â†’
   480â†’### Pattern 4: Performance Monitoring and Observability
   481â†’
   482â†’Enterprise deployments require comprehensive monitoring and alerting capabilities.
   483â†’
   484â†’```python
   485â†’# monitoring/enterprise_monitoring.py
   486â†’import time
   487â†’import asyncio
   488â†’from typing import Dict, List, Any, Optional
   489â†’from dataclasses import dataclass, asdict
   490â†’from collections import defaultdict, deque
   491â†’import statistics
   492â†’import logging
   493â†’
   494â†’logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
   495â†’
   496â†’@dataclass
   497â†’class PerformanceMetrics:
   498â†’    timestamp: float
   499â†’    server_name: str
   500â†’    tool_name: str
   501â†’    response_time: float
   502â†’    success: bool
   503â†’    error_type: Optional[str] = None
   504â†’    user_id: Optional[str] = None
   505â†’
   506â†’class PerformanceTracker:
   507â†’    """Enterprise-grade performance monitoring for MCP agents."""
   508â†’    
   509â†’    def __init__(self, retention_hours: int = 24):
   510â†’        self.retention_hours = retention_hours
   511â†’        self.metrics: deque = deque(maxlen=10000)  # Keep last 10k metrics
   512â†’        self.alert_thresholds = {
   513â†’            "response_time_p95": 5.0,      # 95th percentile response time
   514â†’            "error_rate": 0.05,            # 5% error rate
   515â†’            "availability": 0.99           # 99% availability
   516â†’        }
   517â†’        self.alerts: List[Dict] = []
   518â†’        
   519â†’    def record_metric(self, metric: PerformanceMetrics):
   520â†’        """Record a performance metric."""
   521â†’        self.metrics.append(metric)
   522â†’        self._check_alerts()
   523â†’    
   524â†’    def get_server_stats(self, server_name: str, hours: int = 1) -> Dict[str, Any]:
   525â†’        """Get comprehensive statistics for a server."""
   526â†’        cutoff_time = time.time() - (hours * 3600)
   527â†’        server_metrics = [
   528â†’            m for m in self.metrics 
   529â†’            if m.server_name == server_name and m.timestamp >= cutoff_time
   530â†’        ]
   531â†’        
   532â†’        if not server_metrics:
   533â†’            return {"error": "No metrics found for server"}
   534â†’        
   535â†’        successful_metrics = [m for m in server_metrics if m.success]
   536â†’        failed_metrics = [m for m in server_metrics if not m.success]
   537â†’        
   538â†’        response_times = [m.response_time for m in successful_metrics]
   539â†’        
   540â†’        stats = {
   541â†’            "total_requests": len(server_metrics),
   542â†’            "successful_requests": len(successful_metrics),
   543â†’            "failed_requests": len(failed_metrics),
   544â†’            "error_rate": len(failed_metrics) / len(server_metrics) if server_metrics else 0,
   545â†’            "availability": len(successful_metrics) / len(server_metrics) if server_metrics else 0,
   546â†’        }
   547â†’        
   548â†’        if response_times:
   549â†’            stats.update({
   550â†’                "avg_response_time": statistics.mean(response_times),
   551â†’                "min_response_time": min(response_times),
   552â†’                "max_response_time": max(response_times),
   553â†’                "p50_response_time": statistics.median(response_times),
   554â†’                "p95_response_time": self._percentile(response_times, 0.95),
   555â†’                "p99_response_time": self._percentile(response_times, 0.99),
   556â†’            })
   557â†’        
   558â†’        # Error breakdown
   559â†’        error_counts = defaultdict(int)
   560â†’        for metric in failed_metrics:
   561â†’            error_counts[metric.error_type or "unknown"] += 1
   562â†’        stats["error_breakdown"] = dict(error_counts)
   563â†’        
   564â†’        return stats
   565â†’    
   566â†’    def get_tool_stats(self, tool_name: str, hours: int = 1) -> Dict[str, Any]:
   567â†’        """Get statistics for a specific tool across all servers."""
   568â†’        cutoff_time = time.time() - (hours * 3600)
   569â†’        tool_metrics = [
   570â†’            m for m in self.metrics 
   571â†’            if m.tool_name == tool_name and m.timestamp >= cutoff_time
   572â†’        ]
   573â†’        
   574â†’        if not tool_metrics:
   575â†’            return {"error": "No metrics found for tool"}
   576â†’        
   577â†’        # Group by server
   578â†’        server_stats = defaultdict(list)
   579â†’        for metric in tool_metrics:
   580â†’            server_stats[metric.server_name].append(metric)
   581â†’        
   582â†’        result = {
   583â†’            "total_requests": len(tool_metrics),
   584â†’            "servers_used": list(server_stats.keys()),
   585â†’            "per_server_stats": {}
   586â†’        }
   587â†’        
   588â†’        for server, metrics in server_stats.items():
   589â†’            successful = [m for m in metrics if m.success]
   590â†’            result["per_server_stats"][server] = {
   591â†’                "requests": len(metrics),
   592â†’                "success_rate": len(successful) / len(metrics),
   593â†’                "avg_response_time": statistics.mean([m.response_time for m in successful]) if successful else 0
   594â†’            }
   595â†’        
   596â†’        return result
   597â†’    
   598â†’    def _percentile(self, data: List[float], percentile: float) -> float:
   599â†’        """Calculate percentile of data."""
   600â†’        if not data:
   601â†’            return 0.0
   602â†’        sorted_data = sorted(data)
   603â†’        index = int(percentile * len(sorted_data))
   604â†’        return sorted_data[min(index, len(sorted_data) - 1)]
   605â†’    
   606â†’    def _check_alerts(self):
   607â†’        """Check for alert conditions."""
   608â†’        # Only check alerts every 100 metrics to avoid overhead
   609â†’        if len(self.metrics) % 100 != 0:
   610â†’            return
   611â†’        
   612â†’        # Check last hour of data
   613â†’        recent_stats = self.get_server_stats("all", hours=1)
   614â†’        if "error" in recent_stats:
   615â†’            return
   616â†’        
   617â†’        # Check response time P95
   618â†’        if recent_stats.get("p95_response_time", 0) > self.alert_thresholds["response_time_p95"]:
   619â†’            self._trigger_alert("HIGH_RESPONSE_TIME", {
   620â†’                "p95_response_time": recent_stats["p95_response_time"],
   621â†’                "threshold": self.alert_thresholds["response_time_p95"]
   622â†’            })
   623â†’        
   624â†’        # Check error rate
   625â†’        if recent_stats.get("error_rate", 0) > self.alert_thresholds["error_rate"]:
   626â†’            self._trigger_alert("HIGH_ERROR_RATE", {
   627â†’                "error_rate": recent_stats["error_rate"],
   628â†’                "threshold": self.alert_thresholds["error_rate"]
   629â†’            })
   630â†’        
   631â†’        # Check availability
   632â†’        if recent_stats.get("availability", 1) < self.alert_thresholds["availability"]:
   633â†’            self._trigger_alert("LOW_AVAILABILITY", {
   634â†’                "availability": recent_stats["availability"],
   635â†’                "threshold": self.alert_thresholds["availability"]
   636â†’            })
   637â†’    
   638â†’    def _trigger_alert(self, alert_type: str, details: Dict):
   639â†’        """Trigger an alert."""
   640â†’        alert = {
   641â†’            "timestamp": time.time(),
   642â†’            "type": alert_type,
   643â†’            "details": details,
   644â†’            "resolved": False
   645â†’        }
   646â†’        
   647â†’        self.alerts.append(alert)
   648â†’        logger.warning(f"ALERT: {alert_type} - {details}")
   649â†’        
   650â†’        # Keep only last 100 alerts
   651â†’        if len(self.alerts) > 100:
   652â†’            self.alerts = self.alerts[-100:]
   653â†’    
   654â†’    def get_health_status(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
   655â†’        """Get overall system health status."""
   656â†’        recent_time = time.time() - 300  # Last 5 minutes
   657â†’        recent_metrics = [m for m in self.metrics if m.timestamp >= recent_time]
   658â†’        
   659â†’        if not recent_metrics:
   660â†’            return {"status": "UNKNOWN", "reason": "No recent metrics"}
   661â†’        
   662â†’        error_rate = len([m for m in recent_metrics if not m.success]) / len(recent_metrics)
   663â†’        avg_response_time = statistics.mean([m.response_time for m in recent_metrics if m.success])
   664â†’        
   665â†’        if error_rate > 0.1:  # 10% error rate
   666â†’            return {"status": "CRITICAL", "reason": "High error rate", "error_rate": error_rate}
   667â†’        elif error_rate > 0.05:  # 5% error rate
   668â†’            return {"status": "WARNING", "reason": "Elevated error rate", "error_rate": error_rate}
   669â†’        elif avg_response_time > 3.0:  # 3 second average
   670â†’            return {"status": "WARNING", "reason": "Slow response times", "avg_response_time": avg_response_time}
   671â†’        else:
   672â†’            return {"status": "HEALTHY", "error_rate": error_rate, "avg_response_time": avg_response_time}
   673â†’```
   674â†’

<claude_str_replace_old># Session 2: File System MCP Server - Secure File Operations

## Session Overview

In this session, we'll build a production-ready MCP server that provides secure file system operations. Unlike our weather server from Session 1, file operations require careful security considerations and proper error handling.

## Learning Objectives

By the end of this session, you will:

1. **Build a secure MCP file server** with proper access controls
2. **Implement comprehensive error handling** for file operations
3. **Design security boundaries** using allowlists and path validation
4. **Test file operations** safely in isolated environments
5. **Understanding production security patterns** for MCP servers

## Why File System Access?

File operations are among the most powerful and potentially dangerous capabilities an AI agent can have. This session teaches you how to:

- Provide necessary file access while maintaining security
- Implement proper boundary controls
- Handle errors gracefully
- Test dangerous operations safely

## Project Structure

```
file-server/
â”œâ”€â”€ src/
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ file_server/
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ server.py
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ tests/
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ test_server.py
â”œâ”€â”€ pyproject.toml
â”œâ”€â”€ README.md
â””â”€â”€ test_files/
    â”œâ”€â”€ read_test.txt
    â””â”€â”€ subdir/
        â””â”€â”€ nested_file.txt
```

## Implementation

Let's build our file server step by step.

### 1. Project Setup

First, create the project structure and configuration:

**pyproject.toml**
```toml
[build-system]
requires = ["setuptools>=61.0", "wheel"]
build-backend = "setuptools.build_meta"

[project]
name = "file-server"
version = "0.1.0"
description = "MCP File Server - Secure file operations"
authors = [{name = "Your Name", email = "you@example.com"}]
license = {text = "MIT"}
readme = "README.md"
requires-python = ">=3.10"
dependencies = [
    "mcp>=1.0.0",
    "pydantic>=2.0.0",
    "pathlib",
]

[project.optional-dependencies]
dev = [
    "pytest>=7.0.0",
    "pytest-asyncio>=0.21.0",
    "black>=23.0.0",
    "ruff>=0.1.0",
    "mypy>=1.5.0",
]

[project.scripts]
file-server = "file_server.server:main"

[tool.black]
line-length = 88
target-version = ["py310"]

[tool.ruff]
select = ["E", "F", "I", "N", "W", "UP"]
ignore = ["E501"]  # Line length handled by black
line-length = 88
target-version = "py310"

[tool.mypy]
python_version = "3.10"
warn_return_any = true
warn_unused_configs = true
disallow_untyped_defs = true
disallow_incomplete_defs = true
check_untyped_defs = true
disallow_untyped_decorators = true
no_implicit_optional = true
warn_redundant_casts = true
warn_unused_ignores = true
warn_no_return = true
warn_unreachable = true
strict_equality = true
```

### 2. Core Server Implementation

**src/file_server/server.py**
```python
"""
Secure File Operations MCP Server

This server provides controlled file system access through MCP.
It implements security boundaries and proper error handling.
"""

import asyncio
import logging
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any, Optional, List
import json

from mcp.server.models import InitializationOptions
from mcp.server import NotificationOptions, Server
from mcp.types import (
    Resource,
    Tool,
    TextContent,
    ImageContent,
    EmbeddedResource,
    LoggingLevel
)
from pydantic import BaseModel, validator

# Configure logging
logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)
logger = logging.getLogger("file-server")


class FileServerConfig(BaseModel):
    """Configuration for the file server with security controls"""
    
    allowed_directories: List[str] = ["."]
    max_file_size: int = 10 * 1024 * 1024  # 10MB default
    allowed_extensions: Optional[List[str]] = None
    read_only: bool = False
    
    @validator('allowed_directories')
    def validate_directories(cls, v):
        """Ensure all allowed directories exist and are absolute paths"""
        validated = []
        for directory in v:
            path = Path(directory).resolve()
            if not path.exists():
                raise ValueError(f"Directory does not exist: {directory}")
            if not path.is_dir():
                raise ValueError(f"Path is not a directory: {directory}")
            validated.append(str(path))
        return validated


class SecureFileServer:
    """
    Secure MCP file server with configurable access controls.
    
    This server provides file operations while enforcing security boundaries
    through allowlists, size limits, and path validation.
    """
    
    def __init__(self, config: FileServerConfig):
        self.config = config
        self.server = Server("file-server")
        self._setup_handlers()
        
        logger.info("File server initialized with config: %s", config.dict())
    
    def _setup_handlers(self) -> None:
        """Configure all MCP handlers"""
        self.server.list_resources = self._list_resources
        self.server.read_resource = self._read_resource
        self.server.list_tools = self._list_tools
        self.server.call_tool = self._call_tool
    
    def _is_path_allowed(self, file_path: Path) -> bool:
        """
        Check if a file path is within allowed directories.
        
        This implements security boundary enforcement - one of the most
        critical aspects of a file server.
        """
        try:
            resolved_path = file_path.resolve()
            
            for allowed_dir in self.config.allowed_directories:
                allowed_path = Path(allowed_dir).resolve()
                try:
                    resolved_path.relative_to(allowed_path)
                    return True
                except ValueError:
                    continue
                    
            return False
        except (OSError, ValueError):
            return False
    
    def _validate_file_size(self, file_path: Path) -> bool:
        """Check if file size is within limits"""
        try:
            size = file_path.stat().st_size
            return size <= self.config.max_file_size
        except OSError:
            return False
    
    def _validate_extension(self, file_path: Path) -> bool:
        """Check if file extension is allowed"""
        if self.config.allowed_extensions is None:
            return True
        
        extension = file_path.suffix.lower()
        return extension in [ext.lower() for ext in self.config.allowed_extensions]
    
    async def _list_resources(self) -> list[Resource]:
        """List all accessible files as resources"""
        resources = []
        
        for allowed_dir in self.config.allowed_directories:
            dir_path = Path(allowed_dir)
            try:
                for file_path in dir_path.rglob("*"):
                    if file_path.is_file() and self._validate_extension(file_path):
                        uri = f"file://{file_path.as_posix()}"
                        resources.append(Resource(
                            uri=uri,
                            name=file_path.name,
                            description=f"File: {file_path.relative_to(dir_path)}",
                            mimeType=self._get_mime_type(file_path)
                        ))
            except (OSError, PermissionError) as e:
                logger.warning("Cannot access directory %s: %s", allowed_dir, e)
        
        return resources
    
    def _get_mime_type(self, file_path: Path) -> Optional[str]:
        """Determine MIME type from file extension"""
        extension = file_path.suffix.lower()
        mime_types = {
            '.txt': 'text/plain',
            '.md': 'text/markdown',
            '.json': 'application/json',
            '.py': 'text/x-python',
            '.js': 'text/javascript',
            '.html': 'text/html',
            '.css': 'text/css',
            '.png': 'image/png',
            '.jpg': 'image/jpeg',
            '.jpeg': 'image/jpeg',
            '.gif': 'image/gif',
            '.pdf': 'application/pdf',
        }
        return mime_types.get(extension, 'application/octet-stream')
    
    async def _read_resource(self, uri: str) -> str:
        """Read file content with security checks"""
        if not uri.startswith("file://"):
            raise ValueError(f"Unsupported URI scheme: {uri}")
        
        file_path = Path(uri[7:])  # Remove 'file://' prefix
        
        # Security validation
        if not self._is_path_allowed(file_path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {file_path}")
        
        if not file_path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {file_path}")
        
        if not file_path.is_file():
            raise ValueError(f"Path is not a file: {file_path}")
        
        if not self._validate_file_size(file_path):
            raise ValueError(f"File too large: {file_path}")
        
        if not self._validate_extension(file_path):
            raise ValueError(f"File extension not allowed: {file_path}")
        
        try:
            # Try reading as text first
            content = file_path.read_text(encoding='utf-8')
            return content
        except UnicodeDecodeError:
            # If not text, read as binary and encode as base64
            import base64
            content = file_path.read_bytes()
            encoded = base64.b64encode(content).decode('ascii')
            return f"data:{self._get_mime_type(file_path)};base64,{encoded}"
    
    async def _list_tools(self) -> list[Tool]:
        """List available file operation tools"""
        tools = [
            Tool(
                name="read_file",
                description="Read contents of a file",
                inputSchema={
                    "type": "object",
                    "properties": {
                        "path": {
                            "type": "string",
                            "description": "Path to the file to read"
                        }
                    },
                    "required": ["path"]
                }
            ),
            Tool(
                name="list_directory",
                description="List contents of a directory",
                inputSchema={
                    "type": "object",
                    "properties": {
                        "path": {
                            "type": "string",
                            "description": "Path to the directory to list"
                        }
                    },
                    "required": ["path"]
                }
            ),
        ]
        
        # Add write tools if not in read-only mode
        if not self.config.read_only:
            tools.extend([
                Tool(
                    name="write_file",
                    description="Write content to a file",
                    inputSchema={
                        "type": "object",
                        "properties": {
                            "path": {
                                "type": "string",
                                "description": "Path to the file to write"
                            },
                            "content": {
                                "type": "string",
                                "description": "Content to write to the file"
                            }
                        },
                        "required": ["path", "content"]
                    }
                ),
                Tool(
                    name="create_directory",
                    description="Create a new directory",
                    inputSchema={
                        "type": "object",
                        "properties": {
                            "path": {
                                "type": "string",
                                "description": "Path to the directory to create"
                            }
                        },
                        "required": ["path"]
                    }
                ),
                Tool(
                    name="delete_file",
                    description="Delete a file",
                    inputSchema={
                        "type": "object",
                        "properties": {
                            "path": {
                                "type": "string",
                                "description": "Path to the file to delete"
                            }
                        },
                        "required": ["path"]
                    }
                )
            ])
        
        return tools
    
    async def _call_tool(self, name: str, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Execute file operation tools"""
        try:
            if name == "read_file":
                return await self._read_file_tool(arguments)
            elif name == "list_directory":
                return await self._list_directory_tool(arguments)
            elif name == "write_file":
                return await self._write_file_tool(arguments)
            elif name == "create_directory":
                return await self._create_directory_tool(arguments)
            elif name == "delete_file":
                return await self._delete_file_tool(arguments)
            else:
                raise ValueError(f"Unknown tool: {name}")
        except Exception as e:
            logger.error("Tool execution error: %s", e)
            return [TextContent(type="text", text=f"Error: {str(e)}")]
    
    async def _read_file_tool(self, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Tool implementation for reading files"""
        path = Path(arguments["path"])
        
        if not self._is_path_allowed(path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {path}")
        
        if not path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {path}")
        
        if not path.is_file():
            raise ValueError(f"Path is not a file: {path}")
        
        if not self._validate_file_size(path):
            raise ValueError(f"File too large: {path}")
        
        content = path.read_text(encoding='utf-8')
        return [TextContent(type="text", text=content)]
    
    async def _list_directory_tool(self, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Tool implementation for listing directories"""
        path = Path(arguments["path"])
        
        if not self._is_path_allowed(path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {path}")
        
        if not path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(f"Directory not found: {path}")
        
        if not path.is_dir():
            raise ValueError(f"Path is not a directory: {path}")
        
        items = []
        for item in sorted(path.iterdir()):
            item_type = "directory" if item.is_dir() else "file"
            items.append(f"{item.name} ({item_type})")
        
        result = "\n".join(items) if items else "Directory is empty"
        return [TextContent(type="text", text=result)]
    
    async def _write_file_tool(self, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Tool implementation for writing files"""
        if self.config.read_only:
            raise PermissionError("Server is in read-only mode")
        
        path = Path(arguments["path"])
        content = arguments["content"]
        
        if not self._is_path_allowed(path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {path}")
        
        # Check content size
        if len(content.encode('utf-8')) > self.config.max_file_size:
            raise ValueError("Content too large")
        
        if not self._validate_extension(path):
            raise ValueError(f"File extension not allowed: {path}")
        
        # Create parent directories if they don't exist
        path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        
        path.write_text(content, encoding='utf-8')
        return [TextContent(type="text", text=f"Successfully wrote {len(content)} characters to {path}")]
    
    async def _create_directory_tool(self, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Tool implementation for creating directories"""
        if self.config.read_only:
            raise PermissionError("Server is in read-only mode")
        
        path = Path(arguments["path"])
        
        if not self._is_path_allowed(path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {path}")
        
        path.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        return [TextContent(type="text", text=f"Successfully created directory: {path}")]
    
    async def _delete_file_tool(self, arguments: dict[str, Any]) -> list[TextContent]:
        """Tool implementation for deleting files"""
        if self.config.read_only:
            raise PermissionError("Server is in read-only mode")
        
        path = Path(arguments["path"])
        
        if not self._is_path_allowed(path):
            raise PermissionError(f"Access denied to path: {path}")
        
        if not path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {path}")
        
        if not path.is_file():
            raise ValueError(f"Path is not a file: {path}")
        
        path.unlink()
        return [TextContent(type="text", text=f"Successfully deleted file: {path}")]


async def main():
    """Main entry point for the file server"""
    import sys
    
    # Default configuration
    config = FileServerConfig(
        allowed_directories=["./test_files"],
        max_file_size=1024 * 1024,  # 1MB for testing
        allowed_extensions=[".txt", ".md", ".json", ".py"],
        read_only=False
    )
    
    # Create and run server
    file_server = SecureFileServer(config)
    
    # MCP server transport setup
    from mcp.server.stdio import stdio_server
    
    async with stdio_server() as (read_stream, write_stream):
        await file_server.server.run(
            read_stream,
            write_stream,
            InitializationOptions(
                server_name="file-server",
                server_version="0.1.0",
                capabilities=file_server.server.get_capabilities(
                    notification_options=NotificationOptions(),
                    experimental_capabilities={}
                )
            )
        )


if __name__ == "__main__":
    asyncio.run(main())
```

### 3. Test Suite

**src/tests/test_server.py**
```python
"""
Comprehensive tests for the secure file server.

These tests verify both functionality and security boundaries.
"""

import pytest
import tempfile
import asyncio
from pathlib import Path
from unittest.mock import AsyncMock, MagicMock

from file_server.server import SecureFileServer, FileServerConfig


class TestFileServerConfig:
    """Test configuration validation"""
    
    def test_valid_config(self, tmp_path):
        """Test valid configuration creation"""
        config = FileServerConfig(
            allowed_directories=[str(tmp_path)],
            max_file_size=1024,
            allowed_extensions=[".txt"],
            read_only=True
        )
        assert len(config.allowed_directories) == 1
        assert config.max_file_size == 1024
        assert config.allowed_extensions == [".txt"]
        assert config.read_only is True
    
    def test_nonexistent_directory_error(self):
        """Test error for nonexistent directory"""
        with pytest.raises(ValueError, match="Directory does not exist"):
            FileServerConfig(allowed_directories=["/nonexistent/path"])
    
    def test_directory_is_file_error(self, tmp_path):
        """Test error when directory path points to a file"""
        file_path = tmp_path / "test.txt"
        file_path.write_text("test")
        
        with pytest.raises(ValueError, match="Path is not a directory"):
            FileServerConfig(allowed_directories=[str(file_path)])


class TestSecureFileServer:
    """Test secure file server functionality"""
    
    @pytest.fixture
    def temp_dir(self):
        """Create temporary directory for testing"""
        with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as temp_dir:
            temp_path = Path(temp_dir)
            
            # Create test files
            (temp_path / "test.txt").write_text("Hello, World!")
            (temp_path / "test.json").write_text('{"key": "value"}')
            
            # Create subdirectory
            subdir = temp_path / "subdir"
            subdir.mkdir()
            (subdir / "nested.txt").write_text("Nested content")
            
            yield temp_path
    
    @pytest.fixture
    def config(self, temp_dir):
        """Create test configuration"""
        return FileServerConfig(
            allowed_directories=[str(temp_dir)],
            max_file_size=1024,
            allowed_extensions=[".txt", ".json"],
            read_only=False
        )
    
    @pytest.fixture
    def server(self, config):
        """Create test server instance"""
        return SecureFileServer(config)
    
    def test_server_initialization(self, server, config):
        """Test server initializes correctly"""
        assert server.config == config
        assert server.server is not None
    
    def test_path_allowed_validation(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test path validation logic"""
        # Allowed path
        allowed_file = temp_dir / "test.txt"
        assert server._is_path_allowed(allowed_file) is True
        
        # Disallowed path (outside allowed directories)
        disallowed_file = Path("/tmp/outside.txt")
        assert server._is_path_allowed(disallowed_file) is False
        
        # Path traversal attempt
        traversal_path = temp_dir / "../../../etc/passwd"
        assert server._is_path_allowed(traversal_path) is False
    
    def test_file_size_validation(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test file size validation"""
        # Create small file (within limit)
        small_file = temp_dir / "small.txt"
        small_file.write_text("small content")
        assert server._validate_file_size(small_file) is True
        
        # Create large file (exceeds limit)
        large_file = temp_dir / "large.txt"
        large_content = "x" * 2048  # Exceeds 1024 byte limit
        large_file.write_text(large_content)
        assert server._validate_file_size(large_file) is False
    
    def test_extension_validation(self, server):
        """Test file extension validation"""
        # Allowed extension
        txt_file = Path("test.txt")
        assert server._validate_extension(txt_file) is True
        
        json_file = Path("test.json")
        assert server._validate_extension(json_file) is True
        
        # Disallowed extension
        exe_file = Path("test.exe")
        assert server._validate_extension(exe_file) is False
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_list_resources(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test resource listing"""
        resources = await server._list_resources()
        
        # Should find test files
        resource_names = [r.name for r in resources]
        assert "test.txt" in resource_names
        assert "test.json" in resource_names
        assert "nested.txt" in resource_names
        
        # Check URIs are correct
        uris = [r.uri for r in resources]
        assert any("test.txt" in uri for uri in uris)
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_read_resource_success(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test successful file reading"""
        file_path = temp_dir / "test.txt"
        uri = f"file://{file_path.as_posix()}"
        
        content = await server._read_resource(uri)
        assert content == "Hello, World!"
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_read_resource_access_denied(self, server):
        """Test access denied for disallowed paths"""
        uri = "file:///etc/passwd"
        
        with pytest.raises(PermissionError, match="Access denied"):
            await server._read_resource(uri)
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_read_resource_file_not_found(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test file not found error"""
        file_path = temp_dir / "nonexistent.txt"
        uri = f"file://{file_path.as_posix()}"
        
        with pytest.raises(FileNotFoundError):
            await server._read_resource(uri)
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_read_file_tool(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test read_file tool"""
        file_path = temp_dir / "test.txt"
        arguments = {"path": str(file_path)}
        
        result = await server._read_file_tool(arguments)
        assert len(result) == 1
        assert result[0].text == "Hello, World!"
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_list_directory_tool(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test list_directory tool"""
        arguments = {"path": str(temp_dir)}
        
        result = await server._list_directory_tool(arguments)
        assert len(result) == 1
        
        content = result[0].text
        assert "test.txt (file)" in content
        assert "test.json (file)" in content
        assert "subdir (directory)" in content
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_write_file_tool(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test write_file tool"""
        file_path = temp_dir / "new_file.txt"
        arguments = {
            "path": str(file_path),
            "content": "New content"
        }
        
        result = await server._write_file_tool(arguments)
        assert len(result) == 1
        assert "Successfully wrote" in result[0].text
        
        # Verify file was created
        assert file_path.exists()
        assert file_path.read_text() == "New content"
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_create_directory_tool(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test create_directory tool"""
        dir_path = temp_dir / "new_directory"
        arguments = {"path": str(dir_path)}
        
        result = await server._create_directory_tool(arguments)
        assert len(result) == 1
        assert "Successfully created" in result[0].text
        
        # Verify directory was created
        assert dir_path.exists()
        assert dir_path.is_dir()
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_delete_file_tool(self, server, temp_dir):
        """Test delete_file tool"""
        file_path = temp_dir / "test.txt"
        arguments = {"path": str(file_path)}
        
        # Verify file exists first
        assert file_path.exists()
        
        result = await server._delete_file_tool(arguments)
        assert len(result) == 1
        assert "Successfully deleted" in result[0].text
        
        # Verify file was deleted
        assert not file_path.exists()
    
    @pytest.mark.asyncio
    async def test_read_only_mode(self, temp_dir):
        """Test read-only mode prevents write operations"""
        config = FileServerConfig(
            allowed_directories=[str(temp_dir)],
            read_only=True
        )
        server = SecureFileServer(config)
        
        # Write operations should be denied
        arguments = {"path": str(temp_dir / "test.txt"), "content": "test"}
        with pytest.raises(PermissionError, match="read-only mode"):
            await server._write_file_tool(arguments)
        
        arguments = {"path": str(temp_dir / "new_dir")}
        with pytest.raises(PermissionError, match="read-only mode"):
            await server._create_directory_tool(arguments)
        
        arguments = {"path": str(temp_dir / "test.txt")}
        with pytest.raises(PermissionError, match="read-only mode"):
            await server._delete_file_tool(arguments)


@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_server_tool_execution_error_handling():
    """Test error handling in tool execution"""
    config = FileServerConfig(allowed_directories=["."])
    server = SecureFileServer(config)
    
    # Test unknown tool
    result = await server._call_tool("unknown_tool", {})
    assert len(result) == 1
    assert "Error:" in result[0].text
    assert "Unknown tool" in result[0].text


if __name__ == "__main__":
    pytest.main([__file__])
```

## Security Analysis

### Key Security Features

1. **Path Validation**: All file paths are validated against allowed directories
2. **Size Limits**: Files are checked against configurable size limits
3. **Extension Filtering**: Only allowed file extensions can be accessed
4. **Read-Only Mode**: Optional mode that prevents all write operations
5. **Error Handling**: Comprehensive error handling prevents information leakage

### Security Boundaries

- **Directory Allowlists**: Strict control over accessible directories
- **Path Traversal Protection**: Prevents `../` attacks
- **File Size Limits**: Prevents resource exhaustion
- **Extension Validation**: Controls file type access
- **Permission Checking**: Validates access at every operation

## Testing the Server

### Running Tests

```bash
# Install dependencies
pip install -e .[dev]

# Run tests
pytest src/tests/ -v

# Run with coverage
pytest src/tests/ --cov=file_server --cov-report=html
```

### Manual Testing

1. **Start the server**:
   ```bash
   python -m file_server.server
   ```

2. **Test with MCP client** or integrate with Claude Desktop following the same pattern as Session 1.

## Production Considerations

### Security Hardening

1. **Principle of Least Privilege**: Only allow access to necessary directories
2. **Regular Security Audits**: Review access patterns and logs
3. **Input Validation**: Validate all user inputs rigorously
4. **Error Message Sanitization**: Don't leak sensitive information in errors
5. **Resource Limits**: Implement comprehensive resource limits

### Performance Optimization

1. **Streaming for Large Files**: Implement streaming for large file operations
2. **Caching**: Cache file metadata where appropriate
3. **Async Operations**: Use async I/O for better concurrency
4. **Resource Pooling**: Limit concurrent file operations

### Monitoring and Logging

1. **Operation Logging**: Log all file operations with timestamps
2. **Security Event Logging**: Log security violations and access attempts  
3. **Performance Metrics**: Track operation times and resource usage
4. **Alert Systems**: Set up alerts for suspicious activity patterns

## Integration Patterns

This secure file server serves as a foundation for:

1. **Agent Workflows**: Providing file access for AI agent operations
2. **Data Processing Pipelines**: Secure file handling in automated processes
3. **Content Management**: Controlled access to document repositories
4. **Development Tools**: Safe file operations in development environments

## Key Takeaways

1. **Security by Design**: Every operation must be validated and controlled
2. **Defense in Depth**: Multiple layers of security controls
3. **Fail Secure**: When in doubt, deny access rather than allow
4. **Comprehensive Testing**: Test both positive and negative cases
5. **Clear Error Handling**: Provide useful errors without information leakage

The patterns learned in this session apply to any MCP server that handles sensitive operations. The security mindset developed here is essential for production AI agent systems.

## Next Steps

In Session 3, we'll integrate this file server with LangChain agents, demonstrating how MCP servers can be orchestrated in complex AI workflows while maintaining security boundaries.</claude_str_replace_old>

## The Critical Security Threshold

Welcome to the session that transforms you from building safe, sandboxed MCP servers to engineering production-grade systems that handle the most dangerous operations. While Session 1's weather server taught you MCP fundamentals with a harmless API, this session crosses the security threshold into file system operations - the capability that can make or break real AI applications.

File system access represents the moment where MCP servers transition from demonstration tools to production infrastructure. Here, improper security doesn't just mean bad user experience - it means compromised systems, data breaches, and the kind of vulnerabilities that end careers. This session teaches you to think like a security engineer while building the file access patterns that will power every advanced agent system you create.

## Session Overview: Engineering Trust in Dangerous Operations

In this session, we'll build a production-ready MCP server that provides secure file system operations. Unlike our weather server from Session 1, file operations require the security mindset that separates prototype code from enterprise-grade systems. Every line of code you write here embodies the principle that powerful capabilities demand proportional security measures.

By the end of this session, you'll understand why file system access is both essential and dangerous, and how proper engineering transforms this danger into controlled, reliable capability. This foundation prepares you for Session 3's agent orchestration, where multiple MCP servers must cooperate while maintaining security boundaries.

## Learning Objectives: The Production Security Mindset

By the end of this session, you will:

1. **Build a secure MCP file server** with enterprise-grade access controls
2. **Implement comprehensive error handling** that prevents information leakage
3. **Design security boundaries** using allowlists, validation, and fail-safe patterns
4. **Test dangerous operations** safely in isolated, controlled environments
5. **Understand production security patterns** that scale from single servers to agent networks

More importantly, you'll develop the security-first thinking essential for Sessions 4-5's production deployment, where these patterns must operate reliably in live environments.

## Why File System Access: The Power and the Peril

File operations represent the most fundamental yet dangerous capability an AI agent can possess. Consider why this matters:

**The Power**: File access enables agents to read configuration, process documents, generate reports, manage data pipelines, and interact with virtually every business process. Without file system integration, AI agents remain isolated from the real work that organizations need automated.

**The Peril**: Improper file access can expose sensitive data, enable path traversal attacks, cause data corruption, exceed resource limits, and create attack vectors that compromise entire systems. Every security breach has at its heart some form of improper access control.

This session teaches you to harness this power while eliminating the peril through security engineering patterns that you'll apply throughout your AI development career. The techniques you learn here extend far beyond file systems - they represent the security-first mindset essential for any powerful AI capability.

The project structure itself embodies security principles - clear separation of concerns, comprehensive testing, and explicit security boundaries:

## Implementation: Security-First Engineering

Let's build our file server step by step, with each component demonstrating security engineering principles that apply far beyond file operations.

### 1. Project Setup: Production Configuration from Day One
